Davis, on leave, reported the following bill: A Bill To reduce the member and compensation of the officers and others employed at the port of New York. Whereas there were in the employment of the United States, and connected with the collection of the public revenue by impost duties at the port of New York, on the first day of January, one thousand eight hundred and twenty-eight, one hundred and sixty-four persons, and on the first day of January, one thousand eight hundred and forty-two, there were so employed at said port five hundred and two persons; and whereas the annual pay and salaries of said one hundred and sixty-four persons thus employed on the said first day of January, one thousand eight hundred and twenty-eight, amounted to the sum of one hundred and twelve thousand nine hundred and seventy dollars, and the annual pay and salaries of said five hundred and two persons thus employed on the first day of January, one thousand eight hundred and forty-two, amounted to the sum of four hundred and eighty-nine thousand five hundred and twenty-three dollars and fifty-three cents, and whereas the gross amount of revenue collected at said port of New York in the year one thousand eight hundred and twenty-six was eleven million five hundred and eighty-two thousand five hundred and forty-seven dollars and twenty-two cents, and in the year one thousand eight hundred and twenty-seven was thirteen million two hundred and seventy-two thousand five hundred and twenty-six dollars and fifty-four cents, and in the year one thousand eight hundred and forty the gross revenue collected at said port was seven million six hundred and twenty-three thousand and ninety-nine dollars and sixty-six cents, and in the year one thousand eight hundred and forty-one was ten million nine hundred and thirty-two thousand one hundred, and seventeen dollars and ninety-eight cents: Wherefore, ","Committee of the Whole House on the state of the Union"
